<Review>"The Prescott Companies controls homes, condominium & townhouse
communities in Mexico, Canada & the USA." Those living in this type of community only own the inside area of their home - most are worth about $650,000 to
900K+, depending upon where the community is located.
EVERYTHING outside of their unit's boundaries are considered a part of the "common area" and ALL maintenance outside of one's property line, including roofing, painting, road paving,is taken care of by the association.
A few homeowners utilize the greenbelt between Luisito and Salado as a short cut to the northeast exit/entrance gate.
This makes it great for Californians
because, it's the nature of some Californians; many who are self-centered, to walk down this or any greenbelt however, many of the townhouses have downstairs bedrooms; thus, it is imperative to have closed blinds and thick curtains, so a few walker's eyes don't "accidentally wander into one's bedroom?"
Some homeowners, vote every few years to elect the association's "Board of Directors;"each Director must be a homeowner and it's the Board and association that make all the rules that all homeowners must adhere to or possibly face a warning or violation; the fines are either $50 to $100.
The HOA Board of Directors are usually the most seasoned homeowners however, they serve as volunteers, a job where they use their past work experiences/skills in order to serve their community.
Any homeowner may attend their open association meetings however, l've just never felt like I fit in and have only attended one since I've lived here thus, I know very little about what takes place during a meeting.
The HOA also holds "closed meetings" that homeowners may not attend, which I view as sketchy.
NOW, a computerized medium/system called TownSquare, which is how every homeowner communicates with Prescott, the association or eachother, in order to pay bill's, talk about Village matters, etc.,etc.,etc. Through TownSq.,one can use their computers to "talk" about EVERYTHING/ANYTHING that they'd like to see done.
This is the type of living style where some residents don't care to be bothered and very few of them even know their neighbors; I am one of those residents who values my privacy!
In our country, where guns are ablaze everywhere & mass killings have increased in frequency over the last few years, especially within a number of our schools: COVID-19 has only exasperated things yet, too many people - all over the world - are still becoming infected and dying, especially in the poorer countries.
It would be nice to have a Security Station at the entrance or at least a couple of securityguards who both patrol - using a truck - and performing walk throughs?
Then there is the doggie sign that faces my bedroom window & our upstairs balcony where many villagers often brought their dogs to defecate & urinate; by summer & as it gets hot,the high levels of nitrogen in their doggie's urine causes the grass to yellow and then die yet, as long as it's not in front of their unit, I didn't think that most of them cared yet, it seems to have come to a virtual stop over the last few weeks?
It was also very unappealing to watch this senario, while trying to eat on our balcony or through my bedroom window.
Eventually the grass roots die too, leaving a bare circular space of dirt.
A little water might help, during the early morning and late night hours in order to prevent quick evaporation.
The only gate, located at the high northeast end of Luisito and Salado, serves as the only exit/entry for many villagers & before they installed a spring loaded system, it would slam shut loudly & wake me up constantly!
The Friars Village Clubhouse is closed

1.0 star rating 3/8/2017
I normally don't go to shops except in emergencies - I generally like to do most of my auto repair work myself, but sometimes I don't have the time. I've taken my car here twice as the shop is near my house, and both times I've received severely un-satisfactory service. First time was a brake job - needed them to replace front brake lines. Pretty simple but I didn't want to bleed them at home, so I bought in my lines and fluid and asked them to install the lines using the supplied fluid. They did my lines, but didn't use my fluid and charged me for their (probably lower rated) fluid... Also whoever does their brake bleeding should practice BEFORE doing customer cars as the brake feel got worse after upgrading to steel lines from rubber. Second time was just them being lazy - didn't want to align my car "because it is too low" and "it's too much work to get it on the lift" even though I've had it done at multiple shops where my car was also too low, but they put some wood blocks under it for a whopping 15 seconds added to the loading and unloading of the lift. Seem to be more interested in making a quick buck than having return customers. Never taking my business here again. Fooled me once, shame on you; Fooled me twice, shame on me; I'm not getting fooled again.< /review>< user_name>

< Review>
Orangecrest Self Storage has been nothing short of perfect for my family's storage needs. My wife called from the U-Haul truck somewhere on I20, as we moved across country from Texas back home to Riverside. We needed a climate controlled storage for our items, and although at the time Orangecrest Self Storage only had a couple of smaller units available, the price was right, and the property manager, Eric Standing, was very pleasant as we spoke. It wasn't enough for all of our stuff, but it helped with the items that had to be climate controlled, while the rest would have to go to another place. Just in passing I told Eric if a larger unit ever came up to "remember us," because it would be more convenient to have the stuff together. Just a few weeks later the phone rang and it was Eric, saying he'd remembered the comment and he had a larger unit coming up if we still wanted it. The larger unit allowed us to move most all of our stuff into a single unit that didn't accumulate dust, and made it easy to come and go as was needed. Between the price and the excellent service, Orangecrest is the only home for our "stuff," when our stuff can't be at home. Thank you, Eric!<//Review>

< review>
The shopping process was absolutely great!  She spent a lot of time answering our questions and was very helpful in picking out a frame and mattress.  She even steered us to a cheaper mattress model because it was a better fit with what we were looking for.

The ordering process was a bit confusing however.  Their system is quite antiquated and hard to understand.  We ended up double checking the descriptions of what she entered, but eventually we had to just trust it was all correct.

Delivery and setup of the frame and futon was great, but the pillows didn't arrive with the futon.  We were assured they'd be shipped separately.  But a few weeks and phone calls later, the pillows eventually were shipped.  Unfortunately when they arrived, we realized they were incorrect.  A mistake was made when she typed in our order, even though the descriptions were correct.  Once we made them aware of the problem, it took a few more phone calls and they agreed to fix the issue.  However, since the option we thought we ordered was a bit more expensive, they weren't willing to absorb all the cost to fix the mistake.

Overall the shopping experience and setup was great.  However, ordering, follow up, and trying to get mistakes corrected was frustrating.</review>

< Review>
We have been thinking about getting a futon couch for accommodating guest from out of town. I was not sure what the cost would be as I have never gotten one. When we went to the store Sheng was with another customer but greeted us and asked us what we were looking for. When I saw the price tag I was  surprised to see the prices as I they were more expensive than I thought they would be. However, it was Memorial Day weekend and they had very good sales. The organic mattresses looked attractive but they were quite expensive so we went with the standard one.

There are less expensive futon beds out there but the frames are flimsy and the mattresses are not as comfortable. The whole idea of us getting a futon bed is that when guests come over they don't have to sleep on a blow up bed and be comfortable. You get what you pay for.

The wooden frame looks very sturdy and easy to pull out. We had three different choices on color for the frame and we got the black walnut. All of their mattresses and covers are made to order (in SF) so keep in mind there could be 2 to 3 week lead time. It is quite impressive the different fabrics and color you get to choose from for the cover.

We got the standard mattress type and the medium level collection. Sheng helped us pick the right mattress based on the usage. Since they make their own mattresses if your mattress goes bad you can replace it. They do have a 7-year limited warranty though. Or if you want to change the color of the cover you can always purchase a new one.
We had picked a very light cream color but Sheng was kind enough to suggest a darker tint and we got the khaki.

He also mentioned that we should get the rubber pad as you will need it to stop the mattress from slipping. He was very honest with us and said that we can get it for cheaper at Walmart next door as all you have to do is cut it to size. We appreciated the fact that he was straightforward with us but for the price difference, time and effort, it just made sense to get it from them.

The delivery is $70 and only $40 for assembly. We got a queen size futon bed for $1158 including delivery and assembly. Since they have the bed frame in stock, we are getting the futon bed in less than a week. I highly recommend shopping at the Futon Shop if you are looking for quality futon beds.<//Review>

< review>
I couldn't be more pleased with my experience at Hayashida PT, and with my "hero" there, Jason.  I was referred there through my doctor and insurance to treat intense tingling and some pain in my left arm.  About 10 years ago, before moving to Santa Barbara,  I experienced pain in my right shoulder and pectoral muscle,  which was ascribed [via MRI/X-ray examination] to cervical stenosis [i.e. deterioration of the spine at the neck].  While PT solved that immediate problem,  the doctor warned that the long term prognosis was for more serious problems.  So I was pessimistic that the tingling could be due to a pinched nerve at the neck and would require surgery,  something I dreaded,  given my understanding that surgery on the spine can go awry.  Jason reassured me that there was a good probability that stretching and loosening the neck joints [via his manipulation of the neck and assigned exercises] could solve the problem,  and it did!
Further,  the facility on Anacapa St. is pleasant,  quieter and more organized than  some other PT operations I've used over the years.<//review>

<user>104343704169391512963< /user><pictures>None< /pictures><rate>4<//rate><name>Linda Adams<//name>< review>
Inexplicably small quaint quiet coffee shop that punches above its weight class with exceptionally great dishes.  While the exterior seems to portray a cute trendy coffee shop the food is what delivers.  The coffee was okay, but the omelette and quesadilla were truly something you've got to try.  From the way they present the food with a multitude of colors, the layering of the quesadilla on top of a bed of spinach, the crust of the tortilla to crispy perfection they nailed it.  Loved the presentation of the omelette with the sliced avocados ( I don't even like avocados)to the pairing of fruit.  They did a remarkable job with the flavor, temp and all around presentation of the dishes.  You can tell that they really put the care into preparing the dish.  Now, the prices are steep, the coffee was okay, and the location is a little tough to find parking, but once you take that first bite you will know what the ratings represent.  This place is the real deal and as much as I wanted to get a really good cup of coffee I came away thoroughly by the food.. kudos to Tickly Tree!< /review>

< Text>
I love this place SO MUCH. Prior to eating here I had only had Himalayan food once but it was so extraordinary and I knew I wanted to eat more of it. Tara's is across the street from my dentist and is always a must stop after. I have only eaten here in Covid times, and I feel super comfortable doing so. I would love to know what it is like in non pandemic times. I have eaten on the patio which is nice but today it was too cold so I took my food to go. The chana masala and aloo gobi are fantastic but I live for the daal. After eating their daal, I attempted to make them at home and could never replicate the deliciousness of Tara's.

The staff has always been very kind, open, and informative. I have watched them interact with all types of people and there seems to be a really natural accord. As someone who isn't very familiar with the food they serve, they always answer all my questions and help me decide to get that day. I would recommend eating here to anyone.< /Text>

< Gmap_id>
0x80c2ba374ca8b39b:0x339df28ba971a512</Gmap_id>
<time>1457752294709<//time>< review>
This place is awesome!

I am starting to discover Himalayan food so I'm no authority, but I am a very diverse eater and try lots of cuisines.  This cuisine has obvious influences and some dishes from India and South East Asia but with its own unique style.

My favorite is the Thukpa Sherpa stew which I think is specifically Himalayan food and is red and spicy.  The large bowl is brimming with flavor, vegetables, noodles, and a meat of your choice if you want meat.  I get the yak!

Spiciness scale is 1-10.  I can eat Thai hot and the 7 is perfect for me.  I could possibly go 10 but I prefer 7 and I think most Americans should stay below 5.  The combination of temperature hot and spicy hot will make you leak a bit of water.

But damn this place is amazing!!!  I've had other dishes here too that are excellent so go for anything.

I come here at least twice a month.<//review>

110297628207414964456<//user_id>
< Name>
Brendan John<//Name>
<Date>1567871146818< /Date><Rate>4</Rate>< Text>
Tara's continues to be a solid choice for some authentic Himalayan cuisine (aside from the chicken tikka masala and some of the other entrees). The goat curry with bone (Khasi Ko Masu) was delicious. The thick curry with very little oil and likely no dairy reminded me of a home cooked meal. If you're getting it medium spicy, you'll feel the heat, so get the plain sweet lassi on the side, which I found to be delicious and unlike most other lassi you'll see elsewhere. You'll definitely want the naan to go with the Khasi Ko Masu. The service can be a little slow for a Friday night, but you'll leave a happy camper. Parking is impossible in the area, but after your delicious meal, you'll forget the rage you walked in with.</Text>

Good food; good service.

If you've never tried Tara's, it's basically Indian fare but the spices used are a little different. There are also things like Yak meat on the menu, which is quite good.

They have an extensive vegetarian menu as well. We have been going to Tara's for years and have always been met with great service.</Review>

<Review>Tara's always does a fabulous job.  The food is great. But if you have the time and a little extra for a good tip - STAY. It's like stepping into a new realm. The paintings are beautiful and take you away. The people are so nice and some will chat you up if you'd like. I always feel like time slows down and my worries fall by the wayside. Plus I believe 10% of their profits go towards educating Nepali children (& women?). My favorite meal is Hot Himalayan Tea {I will come by just for tea}, lamb korma, saag paneer, rice, and garlic naan. I enjoy the chicken momos, too. And samosas with chutney. And the yak chilli if you want to try something different. Chicken Tikka, sizzle skillets, eggplant appetizer is different & served chilled but still tasty. Mustard greens. I don't know if you can go wrong here. But be careful about spice. Sometimes mild can border on medium so if spice isn't what you're after, make sure they know to dial down the heat.< /Review>< rate>
5<//rate>
